When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine, then he should be cauterized in the area above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as a fingernail; and he should be cauterized one or two times on the back if necessary; and the cauteries should be curved according to the previously described shape.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and does not conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore, one should make three cauteries around the udder, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the back; and the cauteries should be curved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the socket of the hip joint and displace it due to this cause, the sign is that the affected leg appears longer when measured alongside the other; and one finds the site of the displacement soft, so you must cauterize the disease upon the socket of the hip with a .i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark around the socket as it turns, so that the socket remains within the circle; and the cautery should be like those used for cauterizing the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make .iij large cauteries from the olive-oil lamp, and let the cautery be as deep as all the others; and dress it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, it is from cold and moisture, and the disease is cured by what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the disease of gross humors with stinking pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward he should be cauterized; and the way of cautery is according to two ways: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many ways, among which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip joint 3 triangular cauteries according to this form, and he makes a good depth and large, and there is between each cautery of space the thickness of a thumb, and the cauteries are olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip, so that there are 4 according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, he is cauterized with the cautery of the circle which we have previously said about the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And it is the way that one does in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach the thigh or leg. And if it comes to the thigh and leg, he makes 3 cauteries where the disease says that the pain holds him, and 1 cautery above the ankle joint .4 fingers, on the left side a little; and the cauteries are cuticular, and the thickness of the heart is burned; and if the disease feels that the pain extends to two or near there, he is cauterized where he feels the pain .3 or .4 points with the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if he feels the pain below the knee towards the thigh, have him cauterized with a blade or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you don't leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you don't cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen many who have been cauterized on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted all through the foot. After that, he died from a bellyache.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, cauterize one and then the other, according to this method. // And they told me about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the method: make a piece of iron as big as a little finger at the tip, or a little less, and have it split into wedges, with the space between them the thickness of a finger nail; and let the wedges be an inch apart, and also shaped like nuts, and have a good handle. And here is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and glowing, then apply it to the hip joint of the patient, and turn it onto the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave it for three days; then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the application of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery sparingly because of its fearsome reputation, and few people dare to use it; yet it is one of the best cauteries for those who can endure it, wherever it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes from sitting or impact or from excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter, in none of these appearances is cautery worthwhile except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate that after the patient is relieved of foul-smelling pills or other similar remedies, one should apply a line on their back, where the pain is located, three times marked with incense, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be performed according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you wish, perform .iij. cauteries or .iiij. using the middle-sized cautery tool according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight and painful neck when they wake up, and fear; and you will find it in the last spine of the back, and in us the appearance that comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it being cured, then cauterize it with a cautery needle according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If the cautery turns purple on each part of the spine evenly. And if you see it, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery needle .ij. or .iij. lines apart, and let the points be close to one another. After that, cure the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware of administering cautery in a place where there is swelling that is on top of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain in joints is due to moistors that are expanded throughout each member of the body, and when the pain comes from the feet, which they properly call "podagra", and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cautery in such a way: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need for you to prick on the face of the foot, if you make cautery all around the "point". And if pains come up to the knees and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make cautery over each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries on each part, all olive oil cauteries; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand against it longer than until the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, then administer the cautery that we discussed in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then prick around the wrist 2 lines; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, then prick over each joint and over the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take medicines. For if you give him good care and cleanse the blood, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the root of the syphilis
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When gangrene comes in the feet and the bowels descend into the groin and this is new, then when you see it being cured, he should not eat that day. He should use things that loosen the belly so that the feces exit his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relaxed, and bring them back to your fingers, and sign with ink under the gangrene on the bone of the wrist, and all over a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat up the cautery of which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and oozing pus. Then bring the bowels back to their place; and the minister holds his hand so that they do not return; and treat the thighs well for the patient, and put under him 1 cushion and 1 servant under the thighs, and another one under the foot who makes him hold his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowels do not exit when you do the cautery; so that you do not burn him, and so that through this the patient does not die or get worse.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And the cautery for children should be subtle according to the size of an ear, and for large people as large as their ears; after 3 days cure the area around the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; then cure it with other ointments until he is healthy, and make him lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well sewn together; and his bandages should be tied for a long time so that the bowels do not exit when he tries to walk around.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, work little, and guard against too great fullness of drink and food, and excessive loud speaking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I shall now say something about the treatment of cutting into his shoulder.
de la routure dou ventre	of diarrhoea
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When diarrhoea comes from other bellies and is known, and you see that it is not growing any more, if the patient has a large belly, do one cautery of the fire cautery according to its quantity, and burn the third of the heart; after the treatment according to what we have said. Some of the ancients say that it must be cauterized with the 3-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first mark the armpit and draw a line over the breadth above the diarrhoea, and another across, and hold your hand in between throughout the entire cautery. But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb from falling or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, and medicine does not help, then cauterization is required with a cautery called "point", and the cautery should be adjusted according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its virulence, location, twisting, and pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, do another cautery on top of the previous one, for such a custom exists that it should change in the member nearest to which it is, so you must do cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The head is sometimes cauterized with great care, and especially the diseases that come from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it cauterized, take care if the disease is in its early stages, and if it is healed according to what we have said in the division, and does not stop or persist, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the disease, then do 5 cauteries on the head: 1 at the back of the neck, and another towards the front at the end of the hairline; and 2 on the temples, and one behind on the nape; and let your hand remain so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as much as the scalp comes out so that the vapors of the gross humours can come out; and cauterize it on the wound according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the wound is everywhere scattered; and it is bleeding obviously, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said in the head, and .1. cautery in the nose, and .2. cauteries on the spine of the neck, and .6. cauteries on the spine of the back, and .1. large one on the groin and .1. other nearby, and .2. on the .2. shoulders; and .2. on the armpits, and .2. on the tendons of the feet, and .1. on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the creases of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes make .1. cautery on the bone of the wrist, and .1. other on the bone of the stomach, and .1. other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And you should know that the more cautery you do, the more it helps, and moves to help; and you should know that the sick person does not feel pain from cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And the cauteries should be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons. After that, treat the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then one should apply cauteries on the limb according to its size; the cautery should be slightly warm and inserted into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with ointments until it is healed. Sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, or back, at the site where the nerve exits that controls the limb, and in this way, the swelling is removed. However, no one should attempt this if they do not understand the anatomy of the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of alder
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" appears, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a warm cautery according to the thickness of the skin, so that the whiteness is removed and its color changes; then treat it with a poultice made of equal parts of bran, lentils, rosemary oil, plantain leaves, colon blood, and almond blood; mix everything together and apply it, covered with a cloth, until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle all around the edge of the cancer. And yet the wise men say that one must also make a cautery in the middle of the cancer; and yet I don't think this is good, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen sometimes; and a more straightforward thing is to cauterize it all around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called  "adubelati", and it is slow to die, either due to the excess fluid it produces or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, very old) and have little blood, or due to the time of year; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it as it is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through, then heat the cautery of which it is made:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that illness which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the skin, and let the cautery be such that the sick person feels it driven out in such a way that the course of the pustule is relieved. After the cure, let it heal perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of illness is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a corrosion or eating away of a limb, for it eats away at the limbs just as fire burns dry wood. If you see this illness in a place that can withstand cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what is appropriate for the location of the illness; then cauterize all over until you reach down to the corruption, and none of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and apply a poultice made with oil onto the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption is removed. After the cure, use ointments to generate flesh. And if you see after three days that flesh is healing, that is good; and if not, then restart the cautery over what remains of the corrupted areas. And this corrosion can sometimes be cured with medicine rather than fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already described the cure for medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that a disease called 'clos' according to our understanding arises in the feet due to cold, and it is a large, malformed growth that blisters the foot. The cautery for this disease can be performed in two ways: with fire or hot water. With fire cautery, you heat up an iron rod as big as a feather quill, made of good steel with thin edges, until it is red-hot, and then apply it all around the nail, turning your hand around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; leave it like this for three days until pus starts to form. Then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows and sea salt, and leave it on overnight. The nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. After that, clean the area with ointment until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they appear on the body and many times in the hands and feet, you should treat them with hot water cautery as follows: take a brass or iron rod, or an iron quill, and place it on the nail and the surrounding area, especially on warts; then place the rod so that it wraps around the nail, and pour a little hot water on it, holding your hand steady and pressing your hand as you turn the rod so that its edge reaches the base of the nail, allowing the hot water to penetrate deeply to the root. Let the patient endure the pain of the hot water for an hour, then leave it be, and it will be uprooted at all its roots. Do this one after another until you extract all those on the body, then clean them with ointments that promote healing.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other [ailments], you should make four cauteries or six on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the penis, and one on the stomach with the olive-oil cautery. It will stop the trembling and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes they appear as boil-like sores on the body, or as stinking pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter. When they first appear, one should make cauteries on each head of the pustule: a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the tip of which is heated in the fire, or of long aristolochia root, or with the lenticular cautery. Sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning as mentioned, and they cannot grow from thereforth, but the surplus matter from which they came is broken, and they are healed; but this should be done after blood-letting.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great bleeding from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to light, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, you must hurry to place your index finger over the wound of the vein, and press it very hard until the blood is quiet beneath your finger, and no drop comes out; then take several olive-wood cauteries, both large and small according to the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and place the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds again when you lift your finger from the wound, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful not to hurt the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stanched itself when the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have described: by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong ligature, or by medicines placed on it that have power to stanch blood; and let it be bound and pressed firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a tight bandage or places something hot on top, or uses similar remedies, will not find much relief if any.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone and there is no doctor or medicine available, he should put his finger on the wound as we have said, and apply pressure until it is stopped up; and he should not remove it but keep it moist with very cold water until the blood is congealed, swollen, and stopped up; and he should then seek a physician for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cauterization with fire or burning remedies, and the properties, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I included that chapter from the head to the feet, and now I will continue this one on the same topic so that it is easier to find what you are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterization, and because of this, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish. Because there are many types of people who come for treatment. Some are so attached to their illness that they would rather die than give it up, and because of the greatness of their folly, one must fear for them.Et il doit avoir paor de tels qui vienent si adroizement et si prest qu’il ne demourent por l’espousseture ne por la medicine que il demourerent por lor malice; et de ces doit on avoir grant paor, car il n’ont remede.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And one must fear those who come so quickly and eagerly that they do not stay for the leechcraft or the medicine, but only for their folly; and of these one must have great fear, for they have no remedy. And there are those who give you their sense and say, "Wait, I am healed"; yet the disease is stubborn. One must not consent to those who come to you with such an attitude, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not open yourself foolishly but wisely to those from whom you can take and receive; and use prognostic and indication in treating your illnesses, for health is turned toward salvation. And this will help you achieve a good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, may our Lord give you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter for you in discussion according to chapters, just as it is before the chapter on cautery, which I discussed for you from the head to the feet, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the childbirth is too strong, it squeezes the baby's head; and sometimes it comes from a relaxed cause that one does not know about.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and in all those I have seen, death soon followed; therefore it seems to me that it would be better to leave the treatment in several stages.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled every day until it could no longer support it; and it had such an abundance of moisture that it died, and this moisture is collected under the bone above the neck, between the brain and the bone; and if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you should split a large opening in the middle of the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and see the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the cavity is deeper and the abscesses are larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the creases of the head opening on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not close again; then you should split the head into three incisions in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all moisture forcefully. After that, press out the openings with linen and powder, and apply wine and oil, leaving it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and cure the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat, reducing the moisture as much as possible until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe where the abscess opens, and the collection of pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens and the pus collects, and cut according to what you are able; and be careful not to cut the artery, for if blood flows and there is an evacuation of moisture, the patient may die from blood loss.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the feet, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is cauterization with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them cut, the patient should face away; then rub the area around the eyes with a coarse cloth until the arteries appear, then hold the patient's neck with a 1-finger grip; then look where the vein bleeds, and the places are after the ears, and they are very close to each other; then sign the places with a cross, then cut both with an sharp spatulum two parts deep so that the vein bleeds up to the bone, and this should be done from the front of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open to the touch, you must measure the quantity of the space of three digits, then cut down and incise to the bone; and that which it is appropriate to put blood outside is six parts, and by chance a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains anything on the bone, so that pus does not come from it, then drain the wound and ligate it, and treat it with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-age diarrhea comes and the catarrh is acute, due to moistures from tears and heat in the temples and ancient delirium and similar things, and it is treated by various methods of medicine and all that does not help him, then we must draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient pulls back the hair of his temples, and feels the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens easily by its pulse and is little repose outside when in some men who are too cold; and if it is reposed, he pulls his neck from some cloth, then rubs the area with some rough cloth, and washes the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum of which there is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scorch the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with tweezers, and cut it well away from the tissues beneath in each part; and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the nail, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two bones. For if it is not cut, the blood will not flow freely throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw off the blood from 1/4 to 3/8 of an inch; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that pus does not come out before the wound heals, and the blood flows gently; then cut away the excess between the two ties in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron cautery until the bones are cut through; and this is the best treatment if the patient does not have fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to dry up moisture, so it is most helpful for moist wounds.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and places it under well-made tent; and when they are taken off, they are treated with dry medicines that cause pus to form, and with tents until it is healed; and if without cutting the artery as far as you work, hasten to cover it by cautery, or employ vitriol and stretch your hand so that the blood is stained; and if you do not have this present, put a bandage on the place so that the blood congeals, and wet the place with cold water so that the blood stops, and stretch it as it should be; and what is best and most gentle in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery knife of 2 parts, but the blade must be well-spaced to retain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives a finger's width of space, and then when you have marked both places, you place the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be spaced apart because they are not soldered by this cautery throughout; and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the top of the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and in his forehead there is pulsation like trembling; and if their eyes are sunken and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen off, and the eyelids are swollen and burned by the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cured contused", and you should do to the patient who has this disease that he has hairs on his forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions is as two fingers in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose, and the other two are two fingers above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on both sides above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound is the size of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have a piece of sponge and a mouthful of rags ready to wipe away the blood, then fill the spatula with two parts of this mixture, from which the form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to be on the temple up to the second incision; and scorch all of the skin between the two incisions up to the sinus that is on top of the bone, then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put into the first incision the instrument that is called "cultellar", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is smooth and not at all sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the incision towards the armpit to the heart, and the lower incision towards the bone, and bind it tightly until it reaches the middle incision. And clamp all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to the heart, and then make another incision in the middle opening to the other side; then draw out the blood equally, and express the site of the wound for the taken blood; then place a tent made of old cotton in each incision, and place moistened cloths in wine and oil and garlic, and guard against hot abscesses forming there; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer a large amount of cool water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment and oil of roses, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When one has an acute cataract that usually occurs, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakened vision, and burnt eyelids; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain, and the patient sneezes; then from these signs you know that those matters and this cataract come from many veins, and the cure for it is to let it be, as it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you must command the patient to look up, then make a large slit in the middle of the forehead, and another from the left temple to the right, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control chewing; when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then pack the two lips of the slit with old cotton, and apply tenting with linen; then bind wet cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until pus starts to flow, then treat it with things that dry up pus, causing the wound to heal.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of flower of wheat and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment from it; and administer it to these wounds to dry up pus throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	from the treatment of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains or a stone or ore; or something flowing, like water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear, whether a pebble or some other object that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in it, then hold the ear towards the sun. If you see the pebble, apply some drops of violet oil or oil of sweet basil, then bring about extraction; and make him sneeze with a smell, and plug his nostrils when sneezing comes on, and bind pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear uppermost. Very often it comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then bring about extraction with fine pincers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then bring about extraction with a fine needle of small wire; and if it does not come out in this way, then make a hook of bronze and insert the end of the hook into the hole of the ear firmly, and stop up what is around the hook with soft wax so that the air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out forcefully, for very often it comes out as we have said. And if it does not come out in this manner, then take some glue from which birds are caught, and put into it some instrument that is appropriate for doing this, and place some cotton around it; then press the glue onto the pebble or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to split the ear so that the abscess and inflammation will come out, and the spasm; and the manner of the splitting is such that you first make the patient lean his head back, and draw blood according to the measure of its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upward, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fatty part from which it depends; and let the split be like a moon, so that you come to the pebble, then extract it according to your ability, and suck it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain which is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply a thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And administer an incision to that grain. But do not do this when you think the grains are moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with thin pincers and a sucking instrument, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case of water that seeps into the ear, the patient should use a sneezing remedy made from ingredients prepared first, and pack the ear with soft cotton. And let him lie on his side with the affected ear facing down. If the water comes out through the ear, all the better. If not, take many small stones according to the size of your finger, heat them in fire until they are warm, and place one end of the stone into the ear, and strike it with another stone from above, and continue striking the stone in the ear with other stones until all the water comes out, as we have said regarding the stone. And if you see that, take a stalk, insert one end into the ear, and heat the other end in fire until the most delicate stalk is burnt; then do the same with other stalks until all the water comes out, as we have said regarding the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an insect, if it is a small body, like a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the division section. But if it is a large body that can be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section on distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if there are any worms, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take a cockerel's comb, from which is taken the dye:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is narrow underneath and wide at the top. And insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the amount of pain from the ailment; then suck firmly on the cockerel' comb; do this frequently until all the worms come out. And if they do not come out, stop up the ear with cotton as I said about the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the extraction of worms, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, from which is taken the dye:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a narrow end and a wider top for distillation; and to press the distillation into the ear use an instrument of well-crafted brass, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around the blade; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you wish, into the cockerel's comb, and let the comb be in the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm as one heats it over the fire; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be so effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	the cleaning of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an eardrum; and the same thing happens to men through the cleaning of a wound, or from pus forming within the ear, and sometimes this cleaning reaches deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is only a little discharge, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear and cannot be seen, it is a matter of painful healing in various conditions, and in this case, one should put the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane appearing, then it is working as it should.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and smooth both in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to pus or the body of the ear, then grab it with thin pins and gently scrape it, until all the pus is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the infection is deep in the ear, take a small, thin razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear. If you feel the infection which the patient feels great pain in hearing, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a tent according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, then take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriated copper on top; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is fitting to pull out the tent and insert another tent moistened with cerotum made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding that are used for distilling remedies.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal of papers
