Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This poultice comes in papers from the herbs when they are moist and dry, so you should spread them with tongs and tweezers, and the top of a spatula from its roots; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without the outer skin, then cauterize with a lens subtlety, and the cautery after the incision is worth moving; and many times they return, as long as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in papers from herbs that look like hail in its shape and hardness, and this is why the disease is called "hail", and it is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the works are as follows: take care if the hail mutates from one side to another, and that is a light thing to know; then they cut it with a pair of scissors, then the skin of each part lightly, then pick it up with tweezers, and peel it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it will not hurt the patient; and if the split is large, then assemble it with a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will restore it immediately and prevent infection.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hematoma is descending into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and hold it with tweezers, and press from both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, that is not a problem; and when the hematoma is pressed, wash the eye with salted water, and cure the place of what exudes pus until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into the paper, and this happens most to children with no adults, and it is very painful for them, and they get the catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at sunlight because their tears flow to their eyes. And because of this, they sleep on their stomachs, and their papers are under their eyelids, moistened by the inflammation and appearance that covers the eye. And when you press it with your fingers and feel the exinach coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head on the lap of the healthy person; and then take .i. linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that exinach contains in each part, and then put it over him; and press with your fingers from both sides, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moistened spatumile, not any larger than the wound made in vein opening; and cut into the skin deeply enough so that you reach the exinach; and in various dispositions, exinach comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove the bandage completely from one side between your fingers, and move your hand back and forth so that it is loose; and be careful not to push into the wound, otherwise you will reach all the way to the eye and cause bleeding.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound opens at the beginning of the slit, gently open it slightly so that it appears; then remove it as we have said, then wet bandages in vinegar and water, place them on the area, and tie with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are those who bruise and put something on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then heal the wound until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the area, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.Et si li maux sont sus le col ou sus la gueule, si fai boires le bestes de vin et de breu, et si tu mets sus le leu oile d’apricot et poudres.
des poilz des papieres	And if the pain is in the neck or mouth, then have the animal drink wine and brew, and apply apricot oil and powder to the area.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers unlike nature, and are enveillit, they harm themselves and bring on various diseases such as laments and the softening of papers and albugine, until it leads to their destruction; and there are four ways to treat this: by cautery with fire, or by medicine water according to what is before the cautery chapter, and it is done either by incision and sewing or by splints, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the affected area in your dominant hand, then hold the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it turns, that's good, but if not, insert a needle with thread through it; and this should be done near the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and weave one thread throughout the entire paper, and then return it to the razing tool; next, make an incision in the area under the paper, under the abnormal hairs, all the way to the spatumile, cutting through the large and small larmier; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, and sign a figure of enche on the paper, like a fuelle of mirte, and the shape should be according to the amount you see the paper rising.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if one needs to cut out a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is, then make an incision all the way to the spatumile along the two lines you signed, starting from the large larmier to the small; and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair, then insert the needle into one of the angles of the wound, and then peel it all off; then bring the two lips together with a sewing needle and fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, and dry up any excess thread on the two eyebrows with any sticky substance you want to use; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the sewing and threads in for three or four days; then treat the wound without sewing, using dry and compressing substances, because the paper will rise as soon as the wound heals and comes together, but sewing is painful (as the ancients say), and this is a job without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another way: and it is that you draw the paper with a figure which is as the myrtle leaf, as we have described, with .iij. inches unfurled according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out what is on top with small scissors evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers and the object is not equal, take a needle and thread it through the figure; then take another thread and thread it through the larger ear lobe, and the second thread through the smaller one, and gather the threads between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift off all the skin you have marked as we have described, then close the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerot
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the paper hairs are reversed; so you must use what we have said about the incision, but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the bones is as follows: you must turn over the parchment and put it inside according to what I have said, and then make two bones by art, and two thin ligatures as long as the parchment and the width of the spine; and cut two heads into two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble them both subtly above what is on top of the parchment of the eye, and strain the two bones out of their two formed parts; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that was strained will die and harden and fall off as it drops by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, then treat it until it heals; and when the wound is sutured and the parchment lifted, the hairs will no longer hurt; and this is the form of the two bones that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedures are such that you pierce a fine needle and thread in with a thin, soft silk thread; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be about a palm long; then arrange another thin silk thread in the case, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in your hand; and have it exposed to sunlight so that the procedures are declared, for this is a subtle and fine procedure, then pierce the needle through the parchment directly onto the hair, drawing it up through the parchment until it reaches the case, and thread that hair into the case, whether there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out straight through the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the hunt from below to the very thread that you ordered for it, until the hunt comes out through the hole above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from the horse's tail, and let it grow with that one, until it is elongated and then you release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pustule of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "alacrati" or pustules occurs in the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural way and one unnatural way. It can come on suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat it if it is natural is that you split the wound and separate the eyelids, and put in there tendrils of flax, and let it lie until it is healed; and you must not use in its treatment anything that dries and restricts. For if you do, the disease will become worse than before; but you should use soft things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altered and sprouted flaxseed are cooked, and daisy-flower ointments melted in one of the eyes, and wrap a tent around it, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is that you take care not to let it heal according to its previous form; and these works that we have described are remedies for this disease so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the pus that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease, which is truly called "axacrati", is a natural and accidental condition. The accident comes from a wound, a split, cauterization, and similar things; and the way to treat it is to take a needle, thread it with a double thread, and insert it into the pus, piercing from one tear duct to the other, so that the threads come out at both corners of the eye; then the pus comes to the surface all around the needle, and the swollen area becomes about the size of a broad bean.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the split, turn the paper over, and make two splits along the edges within the paper; and let the edges of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision you have made, forming angles so that when they are brought together, the shape is like that of the letter "J" in the Greek alphabet; then remove the pus according to the quantity that has collected beneath, from what follows the paper, then bring the two severed parts together and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it with the medicines we have mentioned for softening and tenting, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you should make a clean split under the hairs of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares remedies with all his power so that he makes the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	And suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this soudure occurs in a similar manner to that of the scalp, with the paper above being separated from the white of the eye, and unable to move or perform its natural functions, then you must therefore pierce the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and press it with tweezers until you grab what is open in the sphynctered subtile, which is neither too sharp nor too trench-like, so that the patient cannot bear the pain of the sphyncter being too sharp and bleeding the eye; and make your incision to peel off this union lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and when all of this assembly is healed, they sometimes have watery eyes with a saline solution, and the eye is raised with soft wool; then put a tent made of linen between the paper and the eye, and place moistened wool on top of the eye; and after the third day, use the collyrium and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You should know that there are two types of nail: one is nervy and resembles a hard wart; the other is not nervy but resembles white congealed moisture, which, when touched with iron and pinched as though to break it, cannot be broken by anyone. Both types originate near the inner corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eyelid and obscure all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient should place his head in your lap, then open his eyes; hold the piece of paper in your hand, then grip the nail with small forceps and lift it up; next, take a needle, thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or bull's hair through it, and double over the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, then tie the nail with a thread and lift it up, and scrape along the side of the nail where the eyelid follows the tear duct down to the lash line, then cut the remaining portion at the root of the tear duct, carefully and with small forces, until you reach the delicate sphincter; leave the natural tissue of the tear duct alone so that no incision comes near it. Sometimes only the nail at the inner corner needs to be lifted and tied as described above; then scrape all around the sphincter, for this is where the form lies:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch and break the fleshy membrane, or pierce the eyelid; after the incision, drop a little crushed vitriol into the eye, and place a collar of litarge around the eye, leaving it on until the next day; then treat the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not sensitive and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the hook cannot enter, this nail-like appearance is often cured by medicine; and it grows back as I have described in the section on division. And if you see it covered, then treat the eye of the patient, and take the spatulum, a small and sharp tool, according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently, and if you see that it does not thin out and the cuticle recedes, then drop a collar made of litarge and red copper and ground seal from your mouth into the eye; then stop up the eye until the next day. Then the next day, repeat the other procedure according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as with a hot abscess, then milk it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then repeat the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid causes great harm in the eye, then pierce it with an awl and scoop out a portion but not all of it, so that the body of tears does not enter; then drop into the eye a red collar made from litarge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men, red flesh sometimes grows over the pupil, covering it and pressing against the eyelids, turning them inside out, resembling a rosebud; and the treatment is to have the patient press his head against a healthy person, then open his eyes, and cut away all that flesh with suitable instruments, holding it firmly; then cut away the first piece of flesh, and keep cutting until the end, being careful not to hurt the eye during the operation; and make the incision over the pupil as we described in the incision of the fingernail, and remove the pus with gentle pressure, as this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, then apply eye salve or you may distill red copperas and similar corrosive medicines, and place a pad of egg white over the eye to protect it from hot abscesses; and if anything remains, and the pus is hot, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with cooling remedies; then return to your treatment until it is healed, and likewise do for as many layers of flesh as are affected in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should adapt the treatment to each weak eye according to its natural condition; and for accidental conditions, use an iron instrument in your treatment; and do not insert your finger into any of these treatments until you see that this member can bear that treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Veins are the red ones that are covered under the eye, and they affect the sight and weaken it all day. So, first of all, you must examine the eye to see if anything is wrong with it other than the sebaceous cyst; then, have the patient lean his head back and gently compress those veins at their base according to your judgement, and let the base be pressed firmly in a double fold according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two folds by degrees in one body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then press those veins gently, and draw out the blood drop by drop after each other, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to pierce the eye with the tips of the spatulae, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very skillful in your work so that you do not touch anything but the veins; and when you have done this, distil into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the cyst.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all that in that hour, then make a poultice of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and there is a warm abscess, then begin again according to this method that is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the 'arissati' fistula closely: when you heal it with cautery and hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a hole in it where you must cut into the abscess, removing all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, then there is the cause of this malady; it is called  'aspre chief'  and should be treated by making an incision from one side to the other, puncturing like a file as shown in the present figure.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little while you know that the corruption is gone; and do this several times, then restore the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the site is sewn up and the wound heals, and the body of the bow is sewn up, and remains so for forty days, and it does not open again and no evil happens, then you know that it is healed; if not, there is nothing else to do but to open the fistula at its opening with a needle according to this form: then uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take a 3-pronged iron, and thin out the shaft up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone in front of the wound, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then push down the entire iron so that it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through their vein if they hold their hand over their needle; then restore the site with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the skin grows and hardens, cut the matter at the needle; this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully all around and there is no disturbance to the brain or thinning, then you should ligature the patient; then treat the eye, then place cups or suckers without piercing to draw out, then apply a poultice over the eye made of acacia and aloe and incense and myrrh, and then bind the eye tightly with bandages and clothes; and the manner of the clothes is that you take quite soft clothes, double each in four, and then place one upon another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then tighten it from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the cups to draw out without piercing; then remove the cups and leave the eye tightened day and night, and if the ligature softens, you should tighten it greatly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then restart the poultice and the clothes and the ligature and the cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the bursting of a web
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woven web, then it opens and comes out of the papers like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the part underneath up to the part above, then push another needle where there is a double thread in the part of the eye; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the place of the double thread and tie one part of the web around, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and put a soft lamb's wool on top; and let it be until the threads break with the membrane, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the web in each part by a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes cause much distress, pierce them with a sharp spatule that comes from the bottom of the eye, and dry the white moisture and lower the eyes, and enter in at once; then pull until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati", occurs only in the bowels of the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the appearance of its treatment is that you have the patient sit upright and straight, then hold his head with both hands, and move him so that you can see the bowel coming to your eyes; then let it be fixed there, and do not lower and cover the light, and let the patient see things as he used to. And if it doesn't descend underneath, know that it is water, and if the bowels don't appear as we have said, hold the patient between your hands, then take the sharp spatule and press on the surface of the cornea with it gently until the bowel emerges; and when it is issued, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled with honey, then let it be cured with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of the disease in its division, and what should be done to pierce it; then act according to health. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so that the sun does not reach him, and close and press his healthy eye very tightly; then place the piece of paper over his eye, on your left hand if his eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if his eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if his eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the corona through the thickness of a hair in that part of the eyeball where the lesser tear duct is, then gently insert the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand so that it pierces the eyeball, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and the measure of the way of almagda should be at the bottom of the measurement of the space which is from the pupil up to the end of the iris; and this is the corona of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument where the disease is, then express it under one way after another. If the disease comes out now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, and if the disease rises up the second way, push it down with the instrument, and when it is fixed in there and does not rise, gently withdraw almagda by turning your hand a little bit; then put in the eye a little bit of seal gem, and remove from that eye. Then place over the eye, after washing it, cotton or wool moistened in rose oil, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, put on comfrey with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make a slender incision, then inject alum, as we have said; and when the work is completed, prepare for the patient a dark room where he can sleep on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movement, and take light foods, and do not move his head or to the right or to the left, and let him be bound according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then re-bind him until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten it so that the water rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	if hot abscesses come, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and use that which soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, loosen the sight and put on his face an eyepatch to cover one eye, and let him remain in that dark house. And then go out of the house a little at a time, and return to his case; and know that no disciple should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Persia, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, causing water to flow out, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read of it in any books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them; and they should be made of brass properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the tips of these pliers should be of the same subtlety, and the handles in .iij. angles bent.
de la char sor le neis	of the jaw above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At times, various types of warts grow on the nose, and some appear like scorpions with many feet; and sometimes there are those with a dark color, and others with a light color. For those warts that are light-colored and not dark, you should make the patient sit facing the sun; open their nostrils, and cut off the wart at its root with a very thin pair of forceps, as far as you can reach, until you know that the entire wart is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains which one cannot cover, then open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess occurs, then lances it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is stanched and all the corruption is removed, then pour in wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the ears are affected and moisture extends to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is corruption in the bone above, and the instruments do not reach to cut it out: therefore you must insert a piece of linen thread, about a finger thick, into the nose and let it hang from the nostril to within the mouth; and space the knots one or two fingers apart as it passes through the nostril. Then have the patient hold the part of the thread that comes from the nose in his hand with his thumb, and pull the other end that comes out of the mouth with his other hand, feeling the knots along the thread as it passes through the nostril. Do this until you know that the corruption has been removed, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the corruption. Then place a plug in the nostril made of soft clay for several days until it is healed, and if medicine is needed to dry it out, use such medicine. This is the form of the instrument used to cleanse the nose, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the instruments should be inserted into it; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and fill it with medicine to cleanse the nose; and there should be a handle on the instrument to hold it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the chest
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the head, and it grows and becomes great sores, so much so that it is visible to the eye; therefore, you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place the cautery or burning medicine on it; and if one delays cutting it until it becomes large, take heed whether it is hard, of a dark color, and lacking in feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess, and when one cuts it, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due to pressure rather than a dark color, and you see that one can cut it all away, then drain the patient and cut it without fear, and clean the area of dry, constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should know that when pus comes from one of these broken cartilage structures, it does little good except in some men. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, you should examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then you should split the .ij. lips into one stitch, then cure them until they are healed; and if the lips are torn on both sides, you should scrape away all the dead tissue from their hearts until they heal, then sew together the .ij. lips into a single stitch, and tighten it, and apply powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and place an ointment over the powders, such as a strong or other adhesive ointment, and leave it in place until it falls off on its own, then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the mouth there are hard abscesses inside the lips, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; therefore, you should split the lips, cut into each node, and squeeze it in every part; then apply vitriol powder after incision, until the blood is stanched; then use a poultice of garlic, and clean the area with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of gum bleeding
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus". You should hold it with tweezers and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then place powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders over the wound. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, that is how you treat an abscess.
des sordens	from sorens
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, indicating that corruption has reached the gum, and they smell bad; so you should have the patient hold his head in your hands, and press his teeth so that they are exposed, until nothing remains; and in this way, deal with blackness, yellowness, and other discoloration, until they are cleaned. If what is removed at first bleeding is good, it's fine; if not, then do it again the next day and the third day, until everything is removed. And know that teeth need different forms of instruments to clean them according to what their condition shows, so that the scaler with which one cleans between the teeth has other forms than those with which one cleans the tops of the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache, it is important to wait as long as possible before pulling the tooth, because it is a very serious matter and one should have no excuse for not treating it properly.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Now, when the patient is compelled to draw breath, you must be certain of the tooth that hurts. Often the pain deceives the patient, and he believes it is in a sound tooth, and has the good tooth pulled; and nevertheless the pain does not cease at all until the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already seen this happen many times; and when you are quite certain of the tooth that hurts, you must scrape around the tooth all around to the gum; then you must move it with your fingers or with fine tweezers little by little until it is well loosened, then hold the tweezers firmly; and the patient's head should be placed between your knees, and held so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, extract the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it will not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it slightly into each side, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, you must fill the holes with lint; and hold it tightly with tweezers so that it does not break when you extract it; and you must work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it behind, which often brings greater pain to the patient due to the root remaining, or by breaking the tooth, as we have seen happen many times; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the socket with wine, garlic, and onions; and if there is bleeding, which often occurs, apply crushed vitriol; and if that does not help, cauterize it.Et se li estrais de la gencive et du dent s’an fust passe par le leu que li dent fu trais, si covient que tu le cauterises. Et se li estrais sont grans, si covient que li sainors soit en guarde que il ne morisse; car il n’a point de leu ou sa sangue ne puise demorer, si qu’il ne die por la saigece qu’il a perdut.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shape of the instruments, which are mute when hitting teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you hit the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick, well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the mucus.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, one should apply wet cotton soaked in butter to the area for a day or two, until the gums become soft. Then, use tweezers called "algefri", which resemble a surgeon's pliers; and they should be made like a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with these tweezers, you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali", which is to say, tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root slips out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should use this instrument which has two branches, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large tweezers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Let this instrument be outside so that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master finds by himself his instrument according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if it does not break or pierce the bone, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong enough to hold the bone so that it doesn't slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines. And if there is a protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then cut it out with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears not according to the natural order of the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down. Then pull it out; and if there is pus with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp edge on its end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And push it in and out gently due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a special file as shown in the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file with which needles are made; and gently file the tooth a little at a time by hand, so that it does not move until it chips; then smooth it completely at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, one should file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front tooth becomes loose, whether through a blow or by falling, and the patient cannot chew without spitting it out, and you have treated it with constricting medicines without success; then it must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never moves. The wire should be of a medium thickness, according to the amount of space between the teeth. If you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and wrap it twice around the healthy tooth, then place the wire between the teeth, whether there is one loose tooth or more, until you reach the loose tooth on the other side; then start covering again from where you began, pulling your hand gently and firmly so that it does not move. The ligature should reach the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then grab the wire with a pair of tweezers and tie it off, and assemble them, and reinsert them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, so that it does not cut the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can stay, and if it slips or the wire breaks, tie it with another wire. It will remain like this for its entire life, and this is the shape of teeth and the method of straightening them, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and only a wise and experienced person should do this, because sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from cow bone, and put in where the defect is, and tied as we have said, and it remains and serves like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	There are two types of wounds to the underside of the tongue: one that is present at birth and another caused by a sudden injury. To treat this wound, open the mouth of the patient, hold their head steady with your hand, and lift the tongue; then cover the nerve wound with a large piece of linen so that the tongue is separated from its socket. If there is any swelling or bruising due to an injury, use the unguent of vitriol on the wound, and if blood oozes out, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery tool, which is suitable for this purpose. Once the wound is healed, treat it further until it is completely cured.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it discolored, black, or hardened, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a ulcer; and if it is leaning towards a blister and there is moisture, apply the unguent of spathumile subtil and drain it from both sides. If blood oozes out during your treatment, apply vitriol until it dries up, then return to your treatment until you draw out all the pus.
