Afterwards, wash the area with water and soap, and treat it further until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	At times, bumps form in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "almonds". When you treat them as described in the previous section and they do not heal, take care: if they are small, hard abscesses with a dark color, do not touch them with iron. If they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron either, so as not to cause bleeding; let them be until they burst on their own. If they are white in color and the root is thin, prepare an instrument for probing, but first check if the abscesses are warm and calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, his head in your lap, and the servant grip his hand between his hands and press his tongue against the instrument, which should be made of silver or thin brass, like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	While pressing the tongue against the instrument, you will see the abscess; take the hook and insert it into the almond, pulling it upwards as hard as you can. Bring out any pus with it, then scrape the instrument against the abscess again, so that it forms a point; this is how it should look, like a sharp spike. The head of the instrument should be curved, one end curved in one direction and the other in the opposite direction, very thin, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use tongs, shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other according to the same method, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils develop in the throat, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely, one abscess of small size; and she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the opening which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died in another day or two. And the abscess had grown so much that it had forced open both openings of the nose. I quickly then pierced one nostril with a needle, and drew out a large amount of pus; then I pierced the other nostril and extracted more matter; and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I pierced the abscess with a needle and cut away some of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the opening in her throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; so I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it stopped growing. And I left those parts, and she was in God's hands after me.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye descends to the tear duct, and it is swollen and long, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an 'uve'. When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus of the eye is reduced, and it is thin; and it is round and not long, and it is blood-red or a light color or black, then you should cut into it. For there is great danger in this ailment. Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have described, by its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from underneath, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for cutting into the two almonds. And you should not cut further than the natural limit; for if you cut more, it causes pain and difficulty in speaking. And after the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of having it cut, then you should use a cautery on his tongue without fear. And the way to cauterize is with hot water. And it is done by the patient putting his head in your healthy mouth, and then pressing his tongue against the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and applying live coals so that they are not too hot or too cool; and use this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a stem at its tip where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and you place the instrument with all the medicine on top of the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine flow out of his mouth and do not go down his throat and into his lungs. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it become soft and the sting of the medicine lessen. And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument completely into the cotton on top, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery, do so, and afterwards wash the area around the medicine with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use rose water, and treat it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this way, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and mix them all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. And the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and in the pot there is an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it may be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes is pushed into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is deadened; then repeat often, until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, because many things happen there; and do not do this unless at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an egg yolk inside it, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; because the egg yolk does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine, or some other thing gets stuck in the throat; so you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will get stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have said, take an instrument of salt plaster according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter the throat more easily, and let the head be raised upwards; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it be broken, nor push the bone in; and move so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he is moved where the object is lodged; then he swallows it, or you pull it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	The blood is sometimes healed by medicine, as I said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument that I have described to you. And if you see the blood, then draw it out with a small hook or with fine tweezers suitable for this. And if this does not work, take a long needle and put it in the throat of the patient, then heat the needle with hot iron, and do this frequently. And if the patient is suffocating from water all day, then take a full glass of cold water, open his mouth, and pour it into him without swallowing, moving it around with his hand often; and as soon as the blood touches the water, it will clot.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not clot as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for smoking out the throat; do this many times, for it will soon clot. And the way of the smoking is to put burning charcoal in a pot, and cover the pot with a perforated lid, and place the instrument's head in the hole; then blow your smoke into it, and have the patient put the needle in his mouth and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the blood; and the blood will clot now, and if it does not, then repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salted and dry things, and do not drink water; and then it will soon come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one draws out the blood is, when one can see it, like curved tweezers so that they can enter the throat; and it has a shape like a surgeon's forceps, and it has roughness from limed iron, so that it cannot let go of what it grabs; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many types of abscesses, depending on their appearance, and they differ in terms of their perforation and size. They occur in two main ways: either due to their appearance or because of the location in the body. Abscesses in the head are different from those in the fundament, and abscesses in fleshy areas are different from those that form in joints. Each type requires a specific treatment approach.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the bowel is healthy according to its completion; and there are some that need to be pierced when they become crusty and do not heal according to their completion, such as abscesses that form near joints. For when abscesses occur near joints, and one waits for it to become purulent around the joint, it can often corrupt the ligament and nerve of the joint, causing contraction in that member. If the abscess is near a principal member, and one delays piercing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal member. But if it is near the fundament, one should pierce it so that it may drain and heal without issue. One must not pierce a crusty abscess without digestion being complete, except for those near the fundament, which may become purulent and elongated inside, leading to the formation of a fistula and prolonged healing.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time of piercing an abscess that is mature according to its completion, which is when the pain subsides, the fever decreases, and there is a reduction in swelling, redness, discharge, and discomfort at the apex of the abscess, along with other signs. The piercing should be done at the highest point of the abscess, where there is movement and an opening; it should be pierced from the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all similar locations without fold or crevice.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	For those who suffer from pain in a particular limb, treat the abscess according to that limb. And when an abscess is located in a fleshy area, it is best to leave it until it is fully healed and consolidated, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, you will lengthen the body from which the poison comes, and it will be filled with much filth; and by chance, the lips and depths of the abscess will harden. And for any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs. And one should treat small abscesses with small openings, and large abscesses with large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses, one should cut the skin and cover it when it has become like a drape and is deadened, just as one does with blisters. And there are some that are split into three angles, and some that are covered like a myrrh pouch, like abscesses in the joints; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those that have no head, such as a superficial abscess, should be pierced directly; and when the abscess is large and has formed a great boil, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in one hour but only part of it; then let the abscess drain until the next day, then draw out some more pus; repeat this several times as the pus comes out, until the boil is completely drained. Do this especially for weak patients, pregnant women, young children, or elderly men. For the pus sometimes jumps back into the body with the flow of the pus, which can lead to death without your realizing it. Therefore, be very cautious in using this method; once you have pierced the abscess, clean the wound and see if the wound of the abscess is small; if it is a plain incision, treat it with tents made of linen or old cotton; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, insert a tent into each opening so that they face each other. If you have cut part of the skin and lifted it around the edge, fill it with dry cotton or rag from an old linen shirt without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs due to your treatment, apply cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, use the remedies and treatments I have described earlier in this book; and if it is during winter, and the area is very nervous, place wet tents and clothes soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is during summer, and the area is fleshy, place wet cloths soaked in water, or cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, clean and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and see the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And when a small abscess comes from the head, it is the nature of us who are in webs, like the joints of a spider's web, and there are many similarities. There are some that are fatty and others where there is pus; and there are some that are hard and stone-like, and there is no fear if the artery does not cause opposition. And the actions of the joints are such that you must test them all with the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes later, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, then it is drawn out from above the long bone. And when the moisture is emptied, it is scraped without leaving anything, for it returns as soon as something is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and then repeat with the cotton, as before, on the second and third days, until you know for sure that it no longer remains at night; then cure the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed. And if the abscess contains fat, then cut it according to this shape, from above; and gouge out your fingernails, and scrape all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the coat in which it lies; and if the artery causes opposition, then do as I told you after. And do the same with an abscess that is stony, and in cutting and curing, as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a moist, stony abscess is lighter, for there is less blood. And if some of these abscesses have no moisture, and one came on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a pebble, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had pierced it, they would have made a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming on the head, before those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent part, so that mucous can exit; and they are cured as they ought to be.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses come in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are many and interwoven with each other. And each scrofula is properly within its coat, as we have said regarding the abscess on the head; and there are many appearances of these scrofulae. There are some that contain moisture, and others which are malignant and refuse to heal. Now, when you see one that has a good disposition to touch, and resembles the color of the body, and is smooth all around, and is not adherent to the nerves in the neck, or to the artery, or to the channel, and is not deep; then you should cut it open on top, and scrape away at each side, and if necessary, cut through the two lips of the wound, as we have said regarding abscesses on the head. Then pull gently, little by little, being careful not to cut any nerve or vein, nor to cause any spasm or twitching that would make the hand jerk, and do not go too far in, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein and it will not let you work, put ground glass into the wound, or some powder that stops bleeding, and bind up the wound; then leave it until the abscess is pacified and the wound softens and begins to suppurate. And when the blood has clotted, return to your task, and finish what you have started; then examine at your leisure if there are any small scrofulae remaining, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, do not cut it but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through without causing harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you scrape all of the scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. Then you should proceed to cover the root of it and draw it out, and sew as we have said before. For those scrofulae that hold a superfluity, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce in the same way as previously mentioned, depending on it, then treat with tenting along with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then treat with an ointment that promotes healing, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, the flap of the throat, which is called the "epiglottis", should be cut; and one must not make an incision by this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are affected by the heat of the abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat's canal, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we must split it under three or four small splits, from top to bottom, between two circles, or according to the amount of the split in the soft palate; not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places where it is suitable to split the epiglottis so that there is no bone, and the vessels are long in between.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to the very end, then split the cartilage until he reaches the larynx; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cover the soft palate as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the cutting of the vein of the finger which bleeds through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed that we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and cut all the way to the cartilage without damaging it; then administer remedies that promote scar tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says to do this only until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then grasp the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease had passed, and it passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take a knife, thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the veins in her throat;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it, and I saw that she had not coughed up any blood or vomited anything except through her throat, and the blood was flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and healed it until she recovered;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and had the young lady been bled before she was sick, and returned later to her normal state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "gorge hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of yolk, and it occurs often in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it happens in two ways: natural, and accidental; where nature has no intent.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental happens in two ways, one of which resembles a boil that comes from an artery, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from a vein.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear in it, and one should not operate by forcing anything except in the small one, and test and probe throughout the entire orifice.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like a boil, and it cannot be opened with any force, as one opens boils, and draw it all around its coat, if there is none;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and surround it quickly, and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of us, all of which I will describe their similarities:
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is necessary that I say all the difference between dislocation and joint dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is a persistent fever and heat until the swelling has passed, and the pus has been expelled; then the fever and heat will subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With no heat or fever or pain, and contains a pus sac which is the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to their appearances, either greasy or moist, and of various colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the ulcer, that you test and examine it first with all the instruments which are called "syringes", according to what its shape will allow in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the brain is that you press on the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and slowly turn your fingers, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the membrane, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the trocar, and be careful not to let anything fall out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the flowing moisture is thick, whatever its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the trocar no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, so do this in the shape of a cross, and grab it with tweezers, and gently scrape each side, and watch the skin where it lies that you draw it out healthy with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything is left behind, it will return to bother us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and does not trouble you greatly, then treat the wound with some corrosive powdered medicines, and apply a hot poultice to the wound, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what causes pus to flow out.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beneath is contrary to you or another, hasten and apply powdered vitriol, and let it remain for 2 or 3 days, until the wound suppurates and the blood flow ceases; then return to cover what has remained uncovered during this time.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and they are of 3 kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are 3 shapes that are called "albaret", and 1 that is called "breb"; and there are also 3 kinds: large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses of different sizes.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are also like needles used for piercing sorcerers' marks, made of brass, iron, or silver, and the black-tipped ones are more effective for probing fistula tunnels.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They come in 3 sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of warts are very varied, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and warts that have two curves in three ways as well.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and warts with three curves and warts with only one curve, and they are in three ways as well; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of those that are cut have a sharp point, and some only cut on one side, which can cause bleeding or damage to the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these intrusions are the needles used in surgery, so that the patient does not feel pain when opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling the slices of an onion, according to this form, with which blood is stopped:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes it is put into the place that heals by copious bleeding of veins and arteries; and sometimes they heal according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they become rotten, so that they look like women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen; and if anyone wants to cure them, they should cut according to this form from line b up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then cut through the fat, and fill the wound with ointment, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and let it heal;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags down and becomes soft due to its size, just like it happens to women, then cut through in two places above, through two similar slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one clings to the other at their end, and the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.:
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient will not rest, or because of bleeding, you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it dissolves the remnant and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula nodules, and some contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain pus should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day; then remove the cotton and treat with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofula, they should be treated as we have said for scrofula fissures, and if the wound is closed, a cautery should be administered as mentioned earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is glued together, many times abscesses occur, and likewise there is swelling of the vein and an abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows it is caused by the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you will feel .i. dislocation; and when it is in the vein, there will be a visible swelling;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and at the angles and in the neck and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the use of iron, and in the one who is at the head, one should also avoid it, and in the one who has inflammation of an artery, they should pierce through the skin on the long side;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then perform incision with a scalpel, and carefully cut open the artery, so that it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then push a needle under it and pierce it all the way to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in .2 places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then probe the area between the .2 ties of a trocar until the pus comes out and the abscess is drained;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that dries up the wound, until the bleeding stops;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is on the size of the vein, you must hold in your hand as much of the abscess as you can to the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and thread a double piece of thread through it so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess as I have said, or ligature on one of its two sides with a thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will hold, insert another needle all along the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads tight in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then lance the abscess until the pus flows out, then lance the pus from the chest and leave what is attached.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then administer poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, so do they come to the nerves when they are hurt, or from too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and all joints where there are articulations, and it is a deep abscess, and its colour resembles the colour of the body, and in many cases it occurs without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body but under the skin;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it does not move in any direction - neither forward nor backward, nor downward nor upward - and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron, or else there might be contraction;

des grosses boces pendans	of large dangling
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes they occur in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to their resemblance to ears, with thin roots and thick stems; there are small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw .I. man who had .ii. or bellies that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference in them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were split open, and moisture was running out of them.

З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut into them and found that one weighed 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces. si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has broken
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a hernia comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure in a syphilitic ulcer, and is on the abdomen with some of the bowels protrude, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from the rupture of syphilis and from the protrusion of the bowels, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens through various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed by hand it springs back, and sometimes it retreats, and if constricted, it grows larger at the entrance of the bath and from great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a slight thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict; and if it is due to blood, then it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is attached according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is because of flatulence, then it is enough to touch it, and the work is that you should look at whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary to leave the treatment. For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or bowels, then you should instruct the patient to tighten his belt and stand straight, then sign all around the belly;

dou chancre	from sores [ulcers]
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the different types of sores [ulcers] and how to treat them with medication, including the use of cauterization with iron. We have also mentioned sores that appear in the mouth, and how to care for them. The ancients say that when sores are in places where they can be reached, such as in the breasts or thighs, and similar areas, they should be removed completely when they are new. However, once they become large and old, one should not touch them, as I have never seen anyone heal from them; nor has anyone healed from them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you sometimes purge the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest fullness, then prepare the patient .i. good site for the operation; then cut your onchites or ulcer, and the hair all over, and the bone all over without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and express the site well with your hand or something, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein makes you feel contrary, cauterize it until the blood vessels are stunned; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already discussed the appearances of dropsy, and how the gathering of fluid occurs, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment through medicine, and that which is treated with iron: now only this remains to be said; and one must not use iron in these two appearances: that is, tympany and hydrops, for these are deadly; therefore, when you treat this appearance of dropsy called 'eclites' with medicines, and the cure does not help, if you see that the patient is weak, or has other diseases besides dropsy, such as dysentery and similar things, then do not use iron, for there is doubt in these cases; but if you see the patient is very strong, and has no other disease except dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then you must treat him thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Take the patient directly in your hands, and the assistant presses his belly by thrusting the water to the lowest part of the feet, then take the spathumile according to this shape: It should be trenchant for 2 parts at the tip, but not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor cause bleeding.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then examine whether the dropsy is towards the intestines: you must split under the armpit on the right side for 3 inches straight down; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then the split should be on the left side for 3 inches; and if it is due to the spleen, then it should be on the right, and the patient must not lie on the split so that the fluids do not run into that weak area.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the way through the skin with the instrument and lift your hand up to the entire spathumile between the skin and the syfac as if you were skinning it for about the thickness of a fingernail or an inch; then pierce the syfac until the spathumile reaches the desired location, and that is where the water is, then pull it out, and insert this instrument from which the shape comes: It is similar to a silver needle, made of brass or lightweight iron, and has 1 small hole on the bottom part; and 3 holes on one side, 2 on the other, and 1 on the opposite side; the head is shaped like a feather, and it is the shape of the incision from which scribes cut feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the tip above is the alemele, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it will descend onto the instrument; empty about half or a third, because if you empty more than it needs in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he may fall into a coma, or approach death.

de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without an aperture in the penis, or the aperture is small, or it is not in its place. Then one should pierce it immediately with a very fine spatulum according to this form: then put into the aperture a very fine plug of lead, and ligature it and keep it so for three or four days; and when he wants to make urine, then remove the plug, and he makes urine, and then replace it; and perhaps one should not do it at all, because the urine which comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose foreskin is tight, if they are treated with the remedy of the skin of a young pig, as we have said, it will loosen. Those who do not have the foreskin in its place are constricted, for some are born with the foreskin at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot copulate because the material cannot reach the penis, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to treat it is for the patient to lie on his back, then the head and shaft of the penis are pulled up like a feather, as far as it will go; and take care to prevent bleeding which often occurs, and if it does happen, then stop the flow with that which stops blood flow, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these whitlows come on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are harmful and harmless ones; therefore you should squeeze them gently with a pair of tweezers, and pull out the roots, then clean and dry them, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with тонконгоном until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and stinking, then you should apply cautery to it. When you have burned it, and if the ulcer is on top of the penis, and part of it is within the skin and part outside, then you should remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is healed, cure the one outside. For when you cure them together, the foreskin of the penis is not secure from being pierced, and blackness and corruption come to the penis and the testicles; so cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply ointment made of honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and eggs, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if there is bleeding, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cautery has two uses together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and swollen, then you should tie a string around the penis and urinate among them; and when the skin is shriveled at the tip of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to a wound or an abscess, then you must scrape off the foreskin with an instrument made of copper, until the ligatures are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a painful thing to discuss this, then you should scrape off the foreskin with a sharp spatula made of copper from the head of the penis and the skin; then quickly remove it between two, and place a thin piece of linen dampened in cold water so that it does not shrivel again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.
