ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is a hard lump within, and on the lips, which does not let blisters form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much mucous;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or because the meat is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or because the medicine is not good for the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the nature of the region is to digest late and to be healthy late, and to swell naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already demonstrated all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Then I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula, which is done manually.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	You should know that a fistula can occur in any part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the face, intestines, bladder, or anywhere in the body,The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or any joint of hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs in the principal member, and similarly elsewhere.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this way are of sad healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have described, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you can see it if you take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, then want it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then search with a thin tent of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because lead bends around the crookedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has a narrow opening and you cannot probe it well with a tent,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse through one of its openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture quickly passes from one opening to another, and cleanses;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you can let it bleed as much as you can, and know whether there is bone or nerve involved, and whether it has been bitten by a snake;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for certain where it is located, whether it is distant from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the locations I have mentioned to you, then treat it according to what I have instructed.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the putrefied flesh and corrupted matter within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat the wound until it is healed;
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep and straight, you must pack it as deeply as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put wet tents in the medicine, and push them into the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put on healing ointments until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve causes you grief in your main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, then treat it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat things that are infected with a cautery until they are healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and the wound returns as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the spring;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover it and want to reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way except by fire cautery;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if extracted by an appropriate instrument for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull them out one by one and leave none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture is causing opposition, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it catches fire and becomes moist and charred, and frees the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something causing pus to flow,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it remain until the pus flows around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have an easier time removing the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape off all the blackness until the corruption is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	and then dress the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches down to the bone;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it needs to be bandaged and wrapped all the way up to the rottenness, and then treated until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg:
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that originated within the body:
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the matter went to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and had no reason to fear opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeon through their folly operated so much that the abscesses opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great deal of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and many openings came from which the body bled and moaned;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons treated him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as I was summoned there, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed from the openings with great quantity;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red in colour, like that of a young boy, and had a yellow tint.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent over one of these openings, and then searched all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some veins came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurried and probed one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and piercing, and the corruption went all the way to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be rotten bone, and I believed that there was no other corruption except for what I had taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with hot medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found that the corruption had continued into the bone, which I cleaned and then removed, and then I struggled to heal the area;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but although I tried as much as I could to heal it, when I cut into the bone by about half a palm's width, and removed all of its rottenness,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then he was restored with medicine; and he was healed and sewed up hurriedly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and the work did not need to be recommenced except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For despite the bloodletting, he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and was born a hard lump in the bone, and had good temper and no harm or contrary pain anywhere, neither when sitting nor standing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be bound in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take a ligature and tie it around the head of the bone which is exposed,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and have someone pull it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another woolen bandage larger than the first one, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and hold the head so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the place where you see it is infected, so that the infection does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a board underneath the bone to cover over the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must examine as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and examine again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part [of the body],
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh completely; then place a hot iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then examine from one part of the corruption to the other, and let him examine the area around the corruption a little, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and the bone which contains it on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way to cut it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the wrist of the foot, then that thing is very strong,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must inquire about the corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but do not let the vein or nerve cause you harm.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that there are many different types of bone-cutting instruments and sutures for covering the bones, depending on the position of the bones and the appearance of the wound.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their thickness and their thinness, their length and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of wound with its appropriate instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that your work will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the instrument that you need according to what is appropriate for it.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may suffer dislocation due to internal causes or external forces.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated this erosion with various remedies, but they are ineffective,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cover the affected area up to the site of the erosion,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	in order for the patient to escape death or the greater harm caused by the defect in the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and if there are signs that the limb becomes black, as though it were burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then goes the corrosion of the limb from one member to another,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and affects throughout the body; so you must hasten to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is through the sting of some venomous beasts, such as the scorpion fish and adder and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head of the elbow, then cut it, and do not give him any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, then cut it at the joint so that the corrosion does not come to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is not worth lessening the amount of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do this when rust comes to the foot: if it comes at the first joint, then the claw follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then claw all of the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it climbs up the leg, then claw at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to cauterize the disease so that the patient dies;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cover or bandage the limb is to tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one assistant pulls one of the bonds downward, and another assistant pulls the other bond upward,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the flesh that is between the two bonds to a width of one digit, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover or bandage it, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the bandage does not touch the healthy area,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and brings about other injuries and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then cauterize the site heavily,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a certain man in his sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he experienced a blackness that looked like burn scars;
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion began at the bottom of his big toe, spreading all over his foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot with a bandage and it healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after he had the corrosion on his fingers, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied striking remedies after cleaning the body, but he could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, as long as there was hope of curing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the strength of man was feeble; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and healed his hand with ointment, and was cured;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other remedy to tell you about, if one has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy area, and remains for so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rot and burst, and in this state the bowels remain empty, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as delicate as a thin cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach the bone or nerve, and such a malady is called 'healed'.
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, then it is called a 'fistula'.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the wound is such that you should cut away all the skin around it, and especially when it is superficial, just like a thin cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not be concerned about causing damage to the tissue.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	If you are worried that the skin will become infected, and the infection is not deep,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with scar tissue, thus the treatment with a cautery:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are large, and the bowels which are within them stink badly,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse them with an Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafætida, and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and mix together, cooking in .i. vessel over a fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	then take some of it according to your need, and they mix it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and they use it as an enema on the breast, and compress the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breasts are deflated and the pain is gone.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are enema with ashes water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, you should burn vine wood to make ashes, pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain the mixture and use it as an enema until the breasts are fully deflated.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if he is enema with water and honey where there is a little quicklime ground;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you cleanse it with honey and mead, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the bowels move;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and are sure that the breast is clean,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the enema makes them defecate,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you should apply a soothing ointment made from rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you can enema with other medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties in the section on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	widen it with a knife a little, and insert a tent made from Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basil icon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave it only in one place where the enema can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that is gushing below is above it, then the wound or lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowels are ruptured, then do not let them be sewed up;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot close the breast underneath as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare it in such a way that the bowels go to the lowest place they can,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bow is perfect, do not let a bad arrow be drawn through it.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you want to,

et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what runs from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises above the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is open, and approaches the saints;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	then loosen it in the morning, or midday, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast flows yellow bile after many days, know that the breast does not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons spread after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health approaches. For there are people in whom the poison moves slowly through their body, and others who it affects quickly;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a swollen and indigestible lump appears on the breast after many days, you can be sure that the lump will not burst.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breast is slow to burst and is distant, then apply medicines which are moist in substance but dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as it defines omentum, because there is a large part of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take omentum, and prepare it with rose oil, and the vinegar of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and with the same mixture, thicken honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when omentum is not available,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue a cloth, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer a long aristolache,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celandine, which is like flour of wheat and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or of compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long, and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is deep, and makes impressions in the bones, or in hard tissues, or in soft tissues;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is a wound of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaris is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or the foot, or occasionally occurs in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes infected, and one takes no care, then there comes a bad abscess,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they decay and rot away until they reach the root of the nail, and sometimes they decay entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	it comes to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the shoulder is swollen and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess growth from the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauteries are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail pushes the flesh in, and starts to poke through, and the bleeding,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must put the fire under the nail so that it doesn't push against the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and press it up gently and gently,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top of the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove it all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and throw it away, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decaying, pull it out with a pair of forceps as previously described,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is infected and swollen, and it feels great pain, then you must treat it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the big toe diagonally,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful not to cut into the flesh underneath the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, place something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sore tooth in the jaw
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The teeth that grow in the mouths of some people by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone, and sometimes a tooth,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some are born at the root of the joint, or their origin is in some part of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those which originate in any finger do not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that originate at the joint of the finger sometimes move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the fleshy one is slight in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spathe.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, if he is painful to cure, hold him tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For one who is born at the tip of the tailbone, you must first round off the flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone to a suitable depth, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Judgments that come to both together come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burn from fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Then you should set that joint, so that the bones heal according to their natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you could place them between two thin pieces of wood, until the joint is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sudamen comes to any of his hands with the palm, he catches it as appropriate.
Des vils	Of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are large, enveloped, and filled with melancholy superfluities, which come in various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him sometimes a purgative of collyrium, and then heal it with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of wounds is according to two methods: one is to apply a cautery, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is made in this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then pull the leg of the patient from above the thigh to just below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide cut,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat meat mixed with black vinegar;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which hurts the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The raising of the leg is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in the bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it with fire, and then apply the hot compress directly to the vein from the top of the knee down to the ankle, or in the area below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the base of the nail, and burn the vein on both sides until it is exposed when one feels it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black; and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the needle underneath, so that it is raised from the skin, and then it can be easily removed at the base of the nail,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then pierce the skin in another location, about two fingers away; then burn the skin over the vein until it is exposed,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then move it to the arm, as you have done, and then to another hook, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then take another turn, or several if needed, then lift it, and tie it around the toe of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift it until the second turn, then release it from turn to turn until it is completely loose, then tie it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a needle with two strands of strong thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and you draw it out, and you push it under .i. hair, and you turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't catch, because if it catches, then one cannot pull it or lift it, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it out completely, then place on the site of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is bent and twisted and wrapped together, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if you must split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to open a vein is curved, and it does not cut, so that it opens the vein without cutting.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	It has a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and thus is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm regions where no plants or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	It may also appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that arise under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as snakes and worms do inside the body, between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of this vein's onset are that a great inflammation comes in the leg,The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes, and the vein begins to come out, just like a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the wound is opened, you must wrap it with a piece of linen from one and a half to two inches wide, and tie it tightly,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang down to the leg, and every time that it comes out of place, wrap around it with the linen again, and tie the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	If it is too long, cut off a portion, and wrap around with what remains, but do not cover the root at all until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, it will enter the flesh and cause an abscess and swelling in that place, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this reason it should be treated little by little until the end, and nothing should remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is treated from five to ten fingers' breadth long,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me whose vein had grown ten fingers' breadth long; and when you cover it, it goes into a vein or veinlet, and pierces right through to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and empty the matter within, and administer medicines in the area for several days, then cure it as with an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes there is bleeding from this vein, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or on the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there is much pus and bleeding; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "bovine disease" in our land because it often occurs in oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and the flesh, traveling throughout the body, going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	The patient feels pain wherever the worm goes, as it dislodges the skin where it travels, causing the skin to jump.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is accompanied by various fluids like pus, blood, and other fluids, similar to that found in warts, tumors, and various types of worms.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled, one cannot help but wonder how it feels when it pierces:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong thread, tightly bound,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then grab above and pull outward, and if the worm is embedded deep in the flesh, and you do not remove it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then grab under it and pull outward;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient's body cleansing with solutive medicines for the bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and to avoid meat that causes putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	About pain caused by flatulence:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from one limb to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything, as lively as silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that spot, and settles in the shoulder
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while later it runs through the whole body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it turned around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this disease progress in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I have seen many who wanted to move pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women had dry bodies and exposed veins;
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because this wind is forced to appear;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and swollen veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	take hold of it above and below firmly, and then press until the windiness forced out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the site; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment of those who drive out wind, as with foul pills, and serapium pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the place in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their points is that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those who have .ij. angles, and those who have tongues, and those with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which breaks in any member, breaks according to two ways: or in a principal member, it breaks,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore breaks in any of these members, and the sign of death which I will tell you about below appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not firmly lodged, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of a skull fracture when the arrow pierces the bone and hits the brain, and the pus comes out from above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	are when there is cutting and bleeding and swelling and redness all over, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without a nose or ears; and perhaps loses his speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and the wound weeps white moisture resembling pus, and also drips like blood;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear, then cease the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced into a hard object, not bleeding.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and occasionally the patient becomes mute like the poultry, and their blood runs cold, and they become cold and break out in a cold sweat, and experience syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	you will know without a doubt that death has come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that pierces the lung is that without pain foam comes from the mouth, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and they sigh deeply and seek the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces into the covering of the foot, it is located between the small ribs; and they spit up a lot of phlegm and experience great pain and sighing; and all their limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow hits the gut, by chance something indigestible might escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow hits the belly, and nothing comes out of the intestine but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder and urine escapes and comes out, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is lethal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, spine, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow hit him in the jaw, at the root of the teeth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it out from under the ear lobe, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I treated an arrow that hit him in the eye socket, under the eyelid:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was withdrawn, but its tip remained pointing towards the forest.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with a very light shaft without ears; the king was unharmed and no ill happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he shot an arrow at a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut off the beards, and slenderized it until I shot it, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I treated a man who had an arrow stuck in his back or belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, dislodged it, and removed it entirely, without any ill effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow that has pierced his back and the wound is closed over:
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and left the arrow inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who was shot in the face with an arrow and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And drew an arrow at a prince of the king's house who had an enemy in his eye,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was fully drawn
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the wound after it had been healed for three days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to treat it with a subtle poultice, and I didn't feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain underneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a cooling and digestive plaster to the area, because the ears were swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the tip of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the ointment many times, and re-opened the wound directly, and the patient remained ill for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine to the wound many times, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was sticking out at the site;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied this medicine to the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it healed well within four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then the wound opened so that I could pry it open with tweezers, and it would not close again;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not cease to treat and devise remedies with tools, until one day I took them with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, as I have described it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeon judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and sewed up the wound, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care into what I do not say, for books cannot understand everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters consider well very few things, and those which are present to them and lacking;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they find new remedies, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are lodged according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or elsewhere;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which suddenly exits through the place it enters is an arrow entering into their flesh, and suddenly exits sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not exit immediately, let them leave it as long as the flesh is broken around it, and let the exit be relieved.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot exit, then let them leave it thus for some days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it pops out; if not, pierce around with a thin stick until the surrounding area is stretched, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and penetrates to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents I have described occur in the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it be until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow penetrates to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the joint,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without ill effect, then use the device to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged deeply and cannot be removed, then apply cauterization around the wound, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deeply within the body and cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it to an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then cut as deeply as you can to open up the wound;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you remove the nail which is stuck in it with two parts of the nail that you can reach
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	then break or bend the arrow's ears so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow as you will then have to pull it out with more force.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do this in one go, then leave it until the skin around it becomes toughened, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood causes a contrary effect, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be wary of cutting the nerve and opening the vein, and use your skill to pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient in the same position as when the arrow hit them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the best help you can give them; and if you cannot, then put them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows which have come from elsewhere, where there is an opening through the skin or the flesh is swollen in that spot so it can be seen or felt obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut on top then, as far as the tweezers can reach, and then pull it out; if it won't come out now, cut again later.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand roundly, as far as it goes into the bone, and widen the hole, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it can't come out, then leave it for now, and then try to extract it again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is in the shoulder, it will reach all the way to the shoulder;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the arrow is short, and you want to administer a bandage, then he should administer a bandage with a needle
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the windpipe of the instrument; and then pull out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, then he should administer an instrument with a pointed end to push it out and ease its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has touched, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits in the foot or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut over it, then cut it out;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting into the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then stitch the wound, if need be;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of tweezers used to treat arrow wounds is similar to an owl's beak; here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the tip that grabs is also like an owl's beak,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push on the point of the arrow, as it is shown in the picture:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs to push and to pull it out if it is in there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Veins from which one bleeds are .xxxi., of which there are xvi. in the head,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	there are two points located after the ears, which are called the "two ears of wheat";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are visible in each temple;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, which are called "spirits";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips on the face, and they are called "augerich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and 2 veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is cephalic, and it is from the left side; and people call it the "wound of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people call it the "wound of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people call it the  "wound of the belly", and it is above the bladder,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is the one that is healed, which opens clearly above the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the armpit on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'nesse', which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are .3 veins underneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient cataracts and with emigration;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleed, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's neck with a wrench,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until they appear behind the ears, in two places, dependent from the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place them on your palm and where you feel the pulse underneath, press in;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through both skin and vein well two times with the lance, and let the blood out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then he pulls and binds it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries in the temples, which is good for old migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for sore eyes and blindness, and for the body of tears with pain;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the surgeon if he is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient holds his neck steady, so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel around your anus, and then sign with your hand;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then press the vein near the top of your penis with your index finger, and insert the lance underneath,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and open the vein at the top, and the cup, as you have done in .xii. other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then ligature it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their bandaging and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein on the forehead is just as good for old diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called a 'pricker', whose form is as follows:
