Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the limb does not improve with what we have said, do not remove the splint for three, four, five, or seven days, and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on how well the fracture is healing and how close the bone is to the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then keep it restrained more than before, and the meat will grow larger, as I have said before. And if you see the area drier than it should be, know that no healing can take place there.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Soak the area in warm water when you remove the splint, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little each time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, the limb will heal, and gently shorten what the foolish wound has made long; this is evil, and it is a cowardly work, and I see nothing good in it except to let it rest and work on it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with diverse appearances, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the bone all the way to the sinus cavity underneath the bone, as with an axe or a staff; this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is concussion accompanied by swelling, or fracture, or a blow from a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating to the membrane just under the bone, or on top of the bone; and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as thinly as a hair, and the fracture is small, then this type of fracture is called 'capillare'.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by being hit with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and it causes the bone to break and enter inside, and the location is splintered like how blacksmiths split iron on an anvil; in this case, the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones at their head, like the skull of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens with all these types of fractures that small pieces are dislodged, as with bones; I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we should know all types of fractures through examination, and through the corrupt flesh that is on top of it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one uncovers the bone and rubs it gently, then the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to any bad signs of illness, and if you see any harmful incidents, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, seizures, feverish shivering, eyes bulging and turning red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any shocking incidents and you expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the patient first comes to you and it is winter, then you should remove the splint before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you should hasten to remove the splint before the seventh day so that the flesh underneath the bone does not rot and cause the incidents we have described.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thus: and it is that you grip the head of the wounded man, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and over the wound more gently than you can,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows out when uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, then help as it is suitable, and it is that you fill the wound with moist bandages in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed and there is no more blood flow; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to 2 methods of work: one method is that you cut with a sharp knife directly in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse tools, some narrow and others wide, and are pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce it around, so that you administer tools with chisels, not deeper than to penetrate through the bone of the skull, and it should have above the point a rim or .i. circle, which does not let the point pass through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all skulls; and this is the form of the .iij. ways of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is to put .i. chisel on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the chisel elsewhere a little later, and thus do all around, then cope with the incisions the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this most subtly and gently, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have, such as tweezers, pincers; and beware of touching the brain or the membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, it is necessary to cut away the membrane which is left on the bone with some instrument like an incision, but it must be more flexible and sharper than the other incision;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it remains in the small bones or any scales, then gently remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and his words are as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the open fracture is located; then, once that part is exposed, place under the head of this lens-shaped instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, but the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet upon it, so that you slightly chip away at the bone all around, taking care to avoid the membrane below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is dislocated to the bone, then the bone should be put back into place gently, for one puts the bone back into place without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with a very thin razor, of which you should have various quantities, in order to apply the most suitable one in each place, according to the action and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take first a large razor, and then a thinner one, and do not cease doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hairline fractures and delicate breaks, you should apply treatment according to their nature; and this is something that is not laid out for one who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the ulcer is exposed, then you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another double-folded cloth in two or three layers, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as gently as you can so that you do not put any pressure on the ulcer. Then apply a bandage over it, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold it in place.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Let it remain like this for one or two days, until the abscesses are soothed. Then remove the bandage and treat the wound with medications such as lily roots, and flour made from beans, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things. Make a powder from these ingredients and apply it to the wound, then administer additional medications without biting the area;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and ensure that the wound is clean and free of any foreign objects, as when a bandage is applied over the brain's membrane, it can become irritated and inflamed, causing great harm to the patient. When something biting is placed on the ulcer and then covered, it will cause irritation from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no ill accident comes to the patient, as we have said, for it is certain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine that one has applied, since such power it has, then you must take some honey and three parts rose oil and mix it into a paste with a cloth, and place it on the ulcer;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the jaw above are broken, either by themselves or together, for they are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, then you must stick your little finger or needle into the wound and place the break inside your index finger, and pull it out with force, until the nail regrows according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nail, and cannot come to the place of the finger, then you must put it equally at the top of a piece of wood, rather thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do the same, and be quick to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is healed, then attach to the head of the tent made of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach another from another part, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some say that one should soak the tents in butter, and change them every day. It does not seem good to me, but they should be soaked in egg white and mill powder; then leave the tent until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they attach goose feathers instead of tents, and wrap it in a silk cloth, and keep the fracture still, and the patient breathes through it; do as you like.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if painful abscesses come in the nose while you are working on it, then apply cerot or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little dyer's alkanet.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if they do not come, then apply a plaster with force, made from flour of salsify, and powdered incense, confited with egg white, then apply it gently on swabs, without binding the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with appropriate instruments for this purpose, then clean the wound and stop the bleeding with healing, soothing plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents and apply a pack of plasters, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below and there is no wound in evidence, and only the joint is dislocated without fracture, and not broken in two, so that it is bent inside, one can perceive this easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should insert your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if it is on the left side, insert the right index finger and gently push the joint back into place with the other hand, keeping it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the dislocation of the jaw is dislocated to one side, one should administer an extension of two parts, so that it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the teeth, or a fracture, then bind them with a gold or silver wire, or silk; then apply cerate to the broken mandible, and place a double drape over it; and place a large, well-made splint, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it in place as tightly as possible; and instruct the patient to rest, and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it on the third day, and then put it back into place again; and apply ointment over it, made of powdered millstone with egg white or flour, after you have removed the cerate; and place a thin layer of lamb's wool over the ointment, and if the jaw is not healing, and its condition remains unchanged, leave it as long as necessary until it heals, sometimes within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine it to see if any piece of bone has been displaced; then reset it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and nothing remains inside, then stitch the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the armpit
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The armpit may break in many ways towards the shoulder, and there are three types of breaks: it may be broken and displaced in two places with pieces, which is the easiest to heal; or it may be broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is no wound in the fracture, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the broken collarbone; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break equal in your hands, so that it has neither appearance nor swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, then put under the shoulder of the patient a round piece of cloth, or of woolen cloth, and let it be thick according to your need; and they lift and loosen the collarbone, and hold the cloth in your hand, so that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out of its socket because it is deeply embedded, then the patient should lie on his back, and put under the shoulder a small pillow, and the ministers press the shoulder down, until the bone of the collarbone is raised up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then grasp the break with your hands, and if you find it split, then you must split it open; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, then use this instrument to ward off the skin:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	it resembles a spoon, and is not flat, and should be as wide as it needs to be according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and it has two ends, as you can see, and one is wide and the other narrow, as is the path of the wound that you made when treating the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then pack the wound with lint and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, then moisten a piece of linen in rosemary oil and garlic and wine, and place it over the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The splitting of the bone, when there is no wound or incision, is that you place on the bone a poultice made from milldust and egg white, and place light bandages over it, and put a splint under the shoulder, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then put a double cloth on cotton pads and anoint it; then take a thin steel rod three fingers in width and length, and wind it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the rod on the fracture, and wind the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sore armpit; and reset it in each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture in place properly, and you see clearly that the rod does not move on top of the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligature loosens, restrain it again;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and have the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit to raise the shoulder; then loosen the fracture of the collarbone by raising the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if no evil accident occurs, until twenty days have passed;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then renew the anointing if you see that he needs it, and restrain and leave him like this until he is healed; and she is healed at most in twenty-eight days, and less with some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder dislocates or widens in its socket, and it is not set right except by touch; then set it according to the pattern of the dislocation, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then place ground flour from a mill with egg white, and light bandages, and place on top a double piece of cloth; then place on top a large and thin board, one hand’s breadth wider than the shoulder, and if underneath the board there is any swelling on the shoulder, then use that swelling to pad the board evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it softens, bind it again, and adjust the board if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, then unbind him, and be sure, for it is not a bone that can be set easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, then cut it off, and the bone, and do as we have said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe the hot abscess.Et se l’os tent desoz lou keur, et non pas avant, si fent de la maniere que nos avon dit; et se li espaule ne puet estre restoures, si covient li faire une chire ou une fente en l’espaule selonc la brisure, et le mettre dedens, et puis le brancher selonc la forme naturale, et le brancher fermement, et le deslie; et se li espaule fuert plus largement del keur qu’il ne devoit estre, si covient li faire une chire en l’espaule adons de la fente, si que li espaule siet igalment, et li faire brancher fermement, et le deslie; car il ne pouet estre restouree.
de la brisure dou pis	of the dislocation of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but that rarely happens; it more often breaks at the top. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downward, and the patient experiences great pain, and there is a lack of movement, and he feels cold all over, and may vomit blood, and the hair turns grey in the broken bone, and he feels great discomfort.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a cushion between his shoulders, then press his shoulders together, and bring the ribs closer together with his hands, and carefully adjust the bone to its proper position; then apply plasters and poultices over the fracture site using a delicate salt or some other lightweight substance, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move; and re-wrap the ligament around the back, and tighten it gently, and check every hour if it has softened, and if so, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or an abscess, then do so quickly, loosen the ligament, remove the plaster, and treat according to the nature of the condition; then re-apply the plaster and tighten until healed.
de la brisure des costes	[treatment for a broken rib]
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures occur only in the thick part near the back, and in the front near the chest, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and it feels good when pressed on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is such that you put the fracture in its proper place, just as it should be. And then apply the plaster and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is bent inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lung; and it also causes shortness of breath and vomiting a great quantity of blood, and it is a very serious condition, and the ancient physicians placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly in order to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not agree that hot abscesses will not form if they have not formed already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if he has come, then heal him.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should apply cups to the area to draw out fluid, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cups might attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the tissue.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with warm, moist wool, and place tents between the ribs to create equal pressure all around, then it is cured by the treatment of pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that points towards the wound, and there is doubt in the patient, then one should split above the location of the broken rib, and one should place underneath .i. instrument to ward off the siphacus; and then one must cut the bone and pull gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed. And if hot abscesses come, one should place moistened cloths in rose oil on top of the wound; and while treating the area where the abscess should be, one should lie carefully on their side where they should, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the neck bones, and it can bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if their hands are soft, swollen, and dead-looking, and if they cannot move or straighten them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in most cases, it is a deadly disposition, and if they can move their hands and feel the pain when you stretch or press on them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be healed if proper care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If a similar thing happens to the spine in the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then examine whether his feet are swollen, and see if the accidents are there which are in the hands, and in the back there is flatulence and urination without wanting it; and when he is laid on his stomach, there is urination without wanting it. And when he is laid on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that it is deadly: so do not labor at all in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the case is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, or rose oil, or the yolk of a new egg, until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and he must not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is exposed, it must be covered with a bandage; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat it with ointment in a bandage, until it is healed; and if there is broken bone, which is called the "bone of the cow", grab your left-hand little finger with your right hand, then apply the plaster and bandage it on, if you need to; then bind it, and if there is exposed bone, sew it up, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It occasionally happens that the hip bone is fractured, and if it does, there will be some lessening at the top; and they hurt for a long time, and decline towards the sides, and the patient feels pain in the area, and there is swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, so that you are on the break; and know which end of the bone is broken and its shape; and if the break is at the top only, then put it back in place, so that it is in its natural shape.Et s’il est au chief et a li parmain, si met cele qui es a li parmain a sa natureil figure, tant qu’ele soit au chief; et s’il est a li parmain soulement, si met cele qui est al chief a sa natureil figure, tant qu’ele soit a li parmain.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then let the patient lie on his stomach, so that the restoration of the break is prepared for him.Et s’il est dou lonc et decline au pardedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son costé tant que cele brisure te soit aparillie.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the ointment, and then place a wooden or leather splint on top, and hold the fracture steady so that it does not move; and apply the area below the ribs, until the color is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful abscesses arise, do not touch them until the painful abscesses are soothed, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad incident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The acromioclavicular joint is what is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two methods. One method is that you take a stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie both ends of the stick with two strings, and bend them upward, and press the patient down on a seat; then pour the broken arm over the stick, so that it comes to rest at the bottom, and press one curve of the stick inwards, and then bend it downward over some heavy object or by the minister extending it downward; then place the broken joint together in alignment with his hands, until the fracture returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his armpit and ties his hand to his neck; then command two ministers, one to hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other below to hold tight from underneath with one string, each pulling their respective ends.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tighten one string below the fracture and one above it, and extend each minister to their part. And if the fracture is closer to the head of the shoulder, then you should put a light string underneath the base of the shoulder, and another towards the collarbone, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the collarbone, then a light string should be placed lightly without effort, so that the fracture is aligned with its proper position, and then extend equally from both sides, as it should be, and tighten it if necessary.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a hot abscess comes, do not drain it until the 7th day, and put soft linen in ash and rose oil on the hot abscess until the hot abscess is soothed; then drain it, and the way to drain it is to put the ointment on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and drain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something moves it, or if the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and put on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint 1 digit of space, and let each splint be as wide as it passes the break by 3 digits on each side; then drain over the splints, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, more strongly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the drainage, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it ligature until the 7th day, as we have said; then look at the ligature every 3 days, so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or the pus cannot come to the member because it is too tight. Then loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen it for three days or more; let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and place underneath the shoulder a plain woolen cushion of equal thickness, and every hour during the day or night, check that the broken member does not move or the ligature become slack; then treat him with medicine and give him the food we mentioned earlier, so that the food is subtle at first and becomes thicker as he starts to recover. It is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within 40 days; then one should loosen it and administer baths and ointment treatments to encourage healing. And if the dislocation is severe and closed up, it should remain loose for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius." The ulna is smaller and located closer to the armpit, while the radius is larger and situated below the small bone. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, sometimes only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When small bones are broken, their restoration and healing are easy; but when large bones are broken, the healing is difficult and more painful than when they are broken together. If only a small bone is broken, it should be gently extended and set straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is a large bone, it must be pulled harder; and he should lie on his back, with his hand highest of all, and his small fingers lowest of all, and the patient should be crossed over himself, and a cushion in front of him, so that he suffers no strain. Then the minister should extend his upper arm to the part below his hand, or to one side, and another minister to the other above. And then let the surgeon set it straight according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, let each be placed in its own position, and if any are displaced, hold the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision on the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; let the cure be taken from there.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if, at the beginning of the healing, hot abscesses arise, then apply a bandage of cerote made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and bind a bandage over it gently, so that the hot abscesses are soothed. Then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of mill-powder with an egg, then put on the splints, and let the splint for the fracture be larger and stronger than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more over the fracture than anywhere else, and always loosen it a little as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the string, with which he is bound, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. Then examine the limb and the binding after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes on the limb, then you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb rest and not be bound tightly. Then restart the binding, and if the ligature has loosened and the bone is displaced, or anything else amiss, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you perceive that the nutrients cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the nutrients flow to it, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said come to the patient, do not loosen it until 20 days. or around, then let him hold his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and stirring, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in 30 days, or 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers there are few fractures, and they come only with great force many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should sit upright and straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on the stretched towel, and stretch the minister the broken bones, and put them even ministerially, so that they are well joined; and put the plaster and the poultices, if abscesses do not come, then put a cast according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in 1 linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the abdomen of the plant, make a sphere of fabrics, and instruct the patient to hold it against his broken plant; then hold it with a long strip of fabric, and let the pad be of woolen cloth as large as the palm of your hand, and hold it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the furrow, you should put a pad on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, whether it's the thumb, hold it straight and even as it should be; then hold it with the plant, and if you see, put a small straight pad to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or any other, hold it even, and tie it with the finger next to it; either tie them all together while holding it, which is better, or put a pad on top, as in the thumb; take care in the restoration and in the application of hot abscesses, and treat those that occur, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and one can see this when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is with one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each ligature to its part equally; and that is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then one ligature should be towards the buttock, and the other ligature below the fracture. And likewise, if it is near the knee, then the ligature should be past the knee, and the extension downward; then the surgeon puts the bone equal to its natural position with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then he applies the poultice and the ligature, unless abscesses come from it.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let him calm down and then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a hard bandage folded in two or three layers, and then tie it tightly, so that only the excess material hangs down. Then, turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the shin, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, so that one end of the thread comes out at the top; then, turn the bandage back over the leg and thigh, and place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft rags to make the binding even, and then begin to tie the binding firmly in three or four places around the fracture. The more you go up from the fracture, the looser the binding should be; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you passed through, and tie the three splints that are on top, and then go back down to the end of the thread, until you reach below the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, and then leave it thus, until no abscess or swelling or similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, then loosen it, and treat what comes out of it as we have said many times before; and if there is a bone fragment protruding, then one must remove it if possible; and if not, then one must split the area and draw it out, and treat the wound as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken like this when splints are put on, as in the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, the malady is not cured by this treatment.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored within one day, or a little less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a slit, or one hole, and it happens in all wounds, and without wounds, and this feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back into place as it was before, with its bones aligned so that they can be set; then apply the plaster, and if necessary, use a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar conditions; then treat each accident as appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that there are two bones in the leg; one is called the "mustel" and the other the "foscile." All fractures occur as they do in the arm, and therefore their treatment is the same, as are all the operations.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, then it turns forward.And if the shinbone is broken, it turns backward. And if the thighbone is broken, it turns outward. And if both are broken, it turns inside out.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and it goes underneath. Then bring about extension, and make it equal, and bind the splints equally; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then let the extension be lesser and more gentle; and alleviate according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints which support the leg on both sides, and which are as long as the leg from the knee down to below; then wrap two bands around them, one above and one below, and tie the middle also, and at this time the leg will not decline to the right or left, and so it is well; and some administer a board as long as the leg, and it is of wood, and they place the leg upon it to prevent movement, and properly they do this in the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg each day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at times there is a fracture of the bones of the foot and of the two bones, and there is only bruising in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see the bones sticking out above one another, then put that foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised up; then press them until they return to their places. Then put the ointment and bandages on top, and place a small wooden board with two smooth sides underneath the belly of the foot, and then bind it tightly to the foot in a suitable manner, and then wrap clothes around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place underneath the foot that board which I have mentioned, and tighten it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on top of each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one layer of linen, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let the top of the board press firmly against the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have already said; and treat each case as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone is broken, make her sit up and lean forward, then hold her from behind. Fill the vagina with cotton and insert a stone as big as an egg; then have the woman stand up and loosen her back little by little, whereupon the cotton will come out along with the stone, bringing the broken bone with it. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, replace it. Do this for seven days, and the fracture will be healed. If you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a straw to the opening, and fill the bladder with air by blowing into the straw until it is inflated inside; the vagina will then pull the broken bone back into place. Fill it with cotton and leave it for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the finger is broken in a man or woman, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; these breaks are not hidden from those who apply themselves to this study with attention and read my book. For in many cases, they indicate the right path to restoration: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap it tightly with cloth and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be bled immediately, so that the bleeding we have described bears witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, then apply vitriol again, if you have nothing else; then restart reducing the fracture in that same hour or day, if no abscesses appear.
